  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_931d1b19-037a-490c-bb9a-a79de15f4074'
      });
    }

The latest fin-tastic tale about a feisty half-mermaid introduces a mysterious boy who shares her fate.</b><br/><br/>When Emily Windsnap discovers an old diamond ring during a class hunt for trinkets, how is she supposed to know that the ring is half the key to unlocking an ancient curse by Neptune himself?   <span id="freeText2852830154733128633" style="display:none"><b>Dive in! The latest fin-tastic tale about a feisty half-mermaid introduces a mysterious boy who shares her fate.</b><br /><br />When Emily Windsnap discovers an old diamond ring during a class hunt for trinkets, how is she supposed to know that the ring is half the key to unlocking an ancient curse by Neptune himself? Now, with the ring stuck firmly on her hand, Emily finds herself under a new curse: in just a few days, she’ll cease to be half-human and half-mermaid and must say good-bye to one parent forever. Can she possibly find the other missing ring that will break all the curses? Is there anyone who can help her — before it’s too late?</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127374767" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16866920793948572242">5/5 stars of course (and so far my favorite in the series)<br/><br/><b> When these two rings connect, every action that was a product of anger or hate will cease to exist. And they will be worn only by a man from the sea and a woman from the earth, or the child that will exist from such a couple. And they will forever symbolize true love and its power against every bad thing </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470179917ra/19898396.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There are reasons this book is my favorite in the series, although I love it as a whole. Unlike the others that have the occasional lau</span>
  <span id="freeText16866920793948572242" style="display:none">5/5 stars of course (and so far my favorite in the series)<br><br><b> When these two rings connect, every action that was a product of anger or hate will cease to exist. And they will be worn only by a man from the sea and a woman from the earth, or the child that will exist from such a couple. And they will forever symbolize true love and its power against every bad thing </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470179917ra/19898396.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are reasons this book is my favorite in the series, although I love it as a whole. Unlike the others that have the occasional laugh or the lighting of the atmosphere, this one is purely made of action, worries and Emily's doubts that are deeper than the ocean itself. It focuses on a mysteriously beautiful diamond ring Emily finds one day close to her ship, and realizes she can't take it off her finger. Poseidon, the king of the seas gets furious with Emily's finding and exiles her to a place far, far away, while at the same time throwing her a curse.<br><br>Emily's relationship with her parents is explained. She worries she'll lose one of them (especially her dad) again. Or that they don't love her. She worries she is not worthy of them more than the normal teenagers, and that mostly has to do with the things she went through. In this book, we saw how much of a strong girl Emily is in fact. Despite the young of her age, she was willing to gamble and play everything if there was at least one chance to save the people she loved, even if the waves took her life.<br><br>Another character I came to adore even more when I first read this book was of course Millie. Yes, she used to be a comic relief in the first book, but she became better and better, and I absolutely loved how protective and motherly she was in this one. Shona was also amazing, strong and loyal and always optimistic, despite the fact that Emily is always followed by a cloud. In this book, Emily also met her soulmate ♥<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441620804ra/16130320.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The writing and plot made me cry at least every minute, especially at the end. I sobbed and let the story keep me in its folds, and I also smiled and my heart warmed up by the beautiful ending and the promise that something good is about to happen, even if nothing seems like it.<br><br><b> I forgive you, he shouted at the moon, the sky. But she was gone. I forgive you, he said, and his voice softened into a whisper </b><br><br>Poseidon in this book was a little less of an asshole. I was happy to remember he had a very sensitive side and lots of open wounds that justified his harsh actions.<br><br>I don't know what else to say, since you guys probably are bored to hear how much I love this series. So I'll only say Please Read It. I know it seems childish. But it is so much deeper than someone can understand, so beautifully crafted and so refreshing, like the cool water of the sea. <br><br>Until my next review, see you soon, my beautiful readers ♥<br>Keep fighting for what's right. Keep caring for your loved ones. And never, ever give up, please ♥<br>~Mary<br><br>P.S: EMILY AND AARON MY BABIES ASDFGHKL *rolls away*<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16866920793948572242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/769641-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388643417p2/769641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/769641-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780763638092" href="/book/show/2184779.Emily_Windsnap_and_the_Castle_in_the_Mist">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who like mermaids/fairy tales</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/769641-jen?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer58308983&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58308983" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2368763560084267283">This is the third book in the Emily Windsnap series, a half human half mermaid teenager trying to find her way in life. The wonderful descriptions of the undersea world were back in this book, including a new habitat of the Castle above land that was vividly brought to life. In this book Emily stumbles across a ring while looking for jewels for King Neptune and accessories to be beautiful for his visit. When she puts it on it is a magical ring that she can not remove, she can feel it has a purpo</span>
  <span id="freeText2368763560084267283" style="display:none">This is the third book in the Emily Windsnap series, a half human half mermaid teenager trying to find her way in life. The wonderful descriptions of the undersea world were back in this book, including a new habitat of the Castle above land that was vividly brought to life. In this book Emily stumbles across a ring while looking for jewels for King Neptune and accessories to be beautiful for his visit. When she puts it on it is a magical ring that she can not remove, she can feel it has a purpose and drags her into the adventure. This book was a bit heavier in the magic side of mermaids :( Neptune puts a curse on her which will eliminate one of her sides, mermaid or human, by the full moon. While Millie has always been a fortune teller type person, Emily has often written her off as a quack where in this book she was heavily involved and using Tarot cards and Ouija type situations which bother me personally. It does make the series one I can't recommend in good conscious to my cousins which are the only kids I really associate with. Overall, the adventure was fun, the descriptions were vivid, and she meets a boy who is half and half too so we all know what is coming in the next book right? ;) but the increasing amount of fortune telling/tarot cards/Ouija/etc was disappointing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2368763560084267283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_552304440" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/552304440?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah D" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah D" href="/user/show/18024523-sarah-d">Sarah D</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer552304440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12653383208084547820"> Emily Windsnap is half mermaid half ordinary girl. She loves going to mermaid school and being with her best friend Shona. One day everything changes when she finds a magical ring buried in the sand. One Emily put it on, it won't come off. Then Emily sends Neptune into rage and he curses her and sends her boat across the ocean to an un-none place. When the boat settles down she sees a castle buried in mist. Emily and Shona go out to the castle but the closer they get the father away the castle </span>
  <span id="freeText12653383208084547820" style="display:none"> Emily Windsnap is half mermaid half ordinary girl. She loves going to mermaid school and being with her best friend Shona. One day everything changes when she finds a magical ring buried in the sand. One Emily put it on, it won't come off. Then Emily sends Neptune into rage and he curses her and sends her boat across the ocean to an un-none place. When the boat settles down she sees a castle buried in mist. Emily and Shona go out to the castle but the closer they get the father away the castle is. Emily finds a cave and goes through it and finds herself in the castle. The castle gives her the creeps until she finds a boy named Aaron and they find a way to break the curse (finding the other ring), but times running out and she has to bring the rings together before midnight comes. Dose she make it and break the curse? Read to find out.<br /><br /> The theme of the book is mystery and adventure. I believe that because they have to figure out the antidote to the curse and the are lots of problems they account.<br /><br /> To me the book is really engaging and i was hooked to the book so much it was hard for me to put the book down. I think the book is very creative with curses and adventure and personality. My rating for sixth grade students is a 3 out of 4.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12653383208084547820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_425690885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425690885" />
    <a title="Faye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5530035-faye"><img alt="Faye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525192507p2/5530035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425690885?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye" href="/user/show/5530035-faye">Faye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425690885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6288286048652374382"> Storyline<br/><br/><i> Emily Windsnap and the Castle in the Mist </i> is the third book in the Emily Windsnap series. One morning, Emily and her class find out in school that Neptune, the mer-king, is coming to the school, and they must search for as many jewels and feathers that they can to decorate themselves for Neptune's arrival. Emily and Shona, her best friend in the world, set off to find some jewels. But while Emily is there, she found a ring, a ring with a big diamond on top. But what she didn't realis</span>
  <span id="freeText6288286048652374382" style="display:none"> Storyline<br /><br /><i> Emily Windsnap and the Castle in the Mist </i> is the third book in the Emily Windsnap series. One morning, Emily and her class find out in school that Neptune, the mer-king, is coming to the school, and they must search for as many jewels and feathers that they can to decorate themselves for Neptune's arrival. Emily and Shona, her best friend in the world, set off to find some jewels. But while Emily is there, she found a ring, a ring with a big diamond on top. But what she didn't realise is that such a beautiful ring can cause a lot of trouble...<br /><br /> Comment<br /><br />This is the third book in the Emily Windsnap series, and I loved it! It is gripping, heart-racing and exciting. What is going to happen next? Where are they going to go? Because these questions keep racing through your mind, you find yourself reading page after page and you are whizzing through it! This is a definite good-read. <br /><br /> Rating<br /><br />I have rated this book four stars, because of how gripping and exciting it is. It has beautiful descriptions, so that you can then picture yourself in the scenery, watching everything happening. I can see that the author, Liz Kessler, put all of her heart and work into the book, which I appreciate very much!<br /><br /> Age Group<br /><br />I think that this book would be good for pre-teens, or maybe 10+. I think that the book is very good, but it has some complicated words and descriptions inside, so I think that it is better for the higher age-group.<br /><br /> My Favourite Character<br /><br />I have been trying to think which one out of the two I like best: Emily Windsnap or Shona Silkfin? They are both kind, fun, adventurous... but I do think that I prefer Shona. She <i> is </i> fun, but she is also very careful and aware of what she's doing, where as Emily does what she wants and finds herself in trouble! I think I love both of them evenly, though.<br /><br /> Suggestion to the Author<br /><br />All I can say to the author is to keep up the terrific work! I think that because I love this series so much, I might just consider buying some of her other books! Keep up the good work. <br /><br /><i> Faye xx </i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6288286048652374382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1461784783" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1461784783" />
    <a title="Brigitte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7629066-brigitte"><img alt="Brigitte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449604545p2/7629066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1461784783?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigitte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigitte" href="/user/show/7629066-brigitte">Brigitte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7629066-brigitte?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7629066-brigitte?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7629066-brigitte?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7629066-brigitte?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1461784783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer835704953405307071">My problem with these books is that everything happens very fast in a small amount of pages so it tends to feel rushed, there isn’t much character development, and I personally don’t get as attached to the characters as I’d like to, and Emily Windsnap and the Castle in the Mist was no exception to this. While I liked the second book in the series a lot, this one didn’t particularly stand out for me since it was so similar to the first book in how the plot unfolded (which could’ve been intentiona</span>
  <span id="freeText835704953405307071" style="display:none">My problem with these books is that everything happens very fast in a small amount of pages so it tends to feel rushed, there isn’t much character development, and I personally don’t get as attached to the characters as I’d like to, and Emily Windsnap and the Castle in the Mist was no exception to this. While I liked the second book in the series a lot, this one didn’t particularly stand out for me since it was so similar to the first book in how the plot unfolded (which could’ve been intentional but would the target audience really notice?) :<br /><br />Emily inevitably kicks off the plot by doing something illegal in her world<br />Emily decides she doesn’t need any help from older characters<br />Emily meets a new character who becomes a permanent fixture later<br />Emily pulls off a miracle<br />Neptune forgives Emily’s transgressions because brings out his humanity (bad choice of words, I know)<br />Everyone lives happily ever after<br /> This dynamic isn’t limited to the plot as the characters are also rather static with Emily and Shona going off on their own without even notifying Millie, who obviously ends up worried sick when she can’t find them (can you tell I’m a bit miffed at this behaviour? Because I am). I felt like Aaron’s introduction was a breath of fresh air because he was an entirely new character, but he ultimately left no lasting impression on me.<br /><br />(just like the romance aspect actually)<br /><br />The book did have one redeeming quality however: it really showed how this new life impacted Emily’s family after their honeymoon phase in the second book. Emily’s parents are virtually stranger after 12 years apart and this is finally felt, while Emily prefers spending her time in the sea, where her mother can’t follow; understandably this is hard on her, and I wish there was a section devoted to how Emily’s parents coped with her latest adventure because that gap weakened the ending.<br /><br />All in all, I found the book rather bland. While I would recommend it to its target audience, I don’t think it would hold the interest of older readers because of its incredible similarity to The Tail of Emily Windsnap.</span>
  <a data-text-id="835704953405307071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4855098997053649571">Emily Windsnap and the Castle in the Mist by Liz Kessler is a fantasy must-read for all preteens! It starts when the main character, Emily Windsnap, finds a beautiful diamond ring buried in the sand, so she puts it on... but then she can't take it off! It becomes a burden (it's cursed and magical), and King Neptune, the king of the sea, is not happy (more like infuriated) with Emily... Read the book to find out why he's so angry with her. Since he is so angry, he sets a curse on her which will r</span>
  <span id="freeText4855098997053649571" style="display:none">Emily Windsnap and the Castle in the Mist by Liz Kessler is a fantasy must-read for all preteens! It starts when the main character, Emily Windsnap, finds a beautiful diamond ring buried in the sand, so she puts it on... but then she can't take it off! It becomes a burden (it's cursed and magical), and King Neptune, the king of the sea, is not happy (more like infuriated) with Emily... Read the book to find out why he's so angry with her. Since he is so angry, he sets a curse on her which will result in her never seeing one of her parents again... can she stop the curse?<br /><br />I just LOVED this book. LOVED it. It was very mysterious and interesting. When Emily was trying to get the other ring, and she was trying to swim to Shona, I was so interested that the real world faded away and I was pulled into the story, not thinking about one other thing besides the book (Seriously!)! When Ms. Kessler was describing the ocean and surroundings, she did a great job, too.<br /><br /><br />When a book is by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/93726.Liz_Kessler" title="Liz Kessler" rel="nofollow noopener">Liz Kessler</a>, you know it's going to be great! She always has an interesting fantasy story to tell, whether it's about a mermaid or a fairy or time-traveling. This one happens to be about a mermaid, and it is the third book in the series. Liz Kessler is a great author from England, and she is a very popular author of children's fantasy stories. Never stop writing! :)<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsbykristina.blogspot.com/2011/12/emily-windsnap-and-castle-in-mist-by.html">http://reviewsbykristina.blogspot.com...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4855098997053649571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I started to read this book because it looked very fun and challenging. This book is about a semi mermaid.Her parents, a human and a mermaid, got married and then had her.When she was on land she was human.In water she was a mermaid. <br /> The king Neptune made Millie, her human babysitter, Shona her best friend and herself leave to a faraway place because she brought a memory back to him; a ring. So he banned that kind of marriage. She either had to be mermaid or human.She would loose her best friend, one of her parents, and one of her lives if she didn't find the other ring. <br /> I really liked this book! Id recommend this book to fantasy lovers and people who like mystery.This was a great book! </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8kGSrGpfKeih6VTddNr9DsTvUoPkmrnZO68wIzUmnji9+Elz9TTgW125Qvzl/Qr+OodwcOBxWBRJay0vIEzDKg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EBK0Zb4fmGTjYkOvv2oTJhQgy1ljDtuBTFvPjq6IsW1fq2+6IXRR1x8yVY4uTeTW6kjpqmflOkw+n9KCu+Lsfw==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_183652'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/183652.The_Fairy_s_Return_and_Other_Princess_Tales?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Fairy&#39;s Return and Other Princess Tales<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/13677.Gail_Carson_Levine?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Gail Carson Levine<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.06 avg rating &mdash; 5,001 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2002\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer13932344454248940035\">Ever since Newbery Honor author Gail Carson Levine introduced the magical village of Snettering-on-Snoakes in the faraway Kingdom of Biddle, young readers have been laughing their way through her hilarious retellings of famous and not-so-famous fairy<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13932344454248940035\" style=\"display:none\">Ever since Newbery Honor author Gail Carson Levine introduced the magical village of Snettering-on-Snoakes in the faraway Kingdom of Biddle, young readers have been laughing their way through her hilarious retellings of famous and not-so-famous fairy tales.\n\nNow, for the first time, the six beloved Princess Tales are together in one magnificent volume:\n\nThe high jinks begin in The Fairy\'s Mistake, which pokes fun at a meddlesome fairy whose plans for good go terribly awry. In The Princess Test, the author spoofs the notion that a pea can prove a person\'s pedigree. Princess Sonora and the Long Sleep features a genius of a princess, a hundred years of snooze, two princes, and a flock of balding sheep! Cinderella is a boy in Cinderellis and the Glass Hill, and the glass slipper is a glass hill. In For Biddle\'s Sake, Parsley tries to forget her beloved prince and get used to life as a Biddlebum Toad.
